Falling for the Enemy

by deathwives

Summary

Professor Vidal has always hated Professor Harkness. Agatha's teaching style was wild, chaotic, a party for each class. Rio on the other hand felt a classroom was a sacred space to learn. Not to have dance parties or comedy shows in. The two were opposites, enemies in each other's eyes.

However, one night- Rio finds herself crying in the ice cream aisle after being stood up by her date. To make matters worse? Agatha Harkness finds her there.

Little did Rio know, the best years of her life stood in that aisle with her...

_______________________________

A small few chapter AU fic:)

“Are you fucking kidding me?” 

 

Rio laughed, tossing her phone down on the desk with a loud smack, not caring if the screen shattered or cracked. Frustration flooded through her veins, annoyance picking at every inch of her skin. 

 

“She can’t just up and change everything!” 

 

She exclaimed, her voice strained with desperation for this to all be a nightmare. One she could wake up and shake off as if it never happened. 

 

Jen shrugged, leaning against the edge of her desk with arms crossed. 

 

“It’s Harkness. Lilia lets her get away with murder”

 

Rio scoffed. 

 

“At this rate, she’ll be giving lectures on how to do that” She grumbled. 

 

Agatha Harkness. 

Agatha. Motherfucking. Aggravating. Irritating. Harkness.

 

Rio shook her head, thinking over the name that made her bones shiver, jaw clench till every muscle in her was so tense- they were all close to exploding louder than any sound in the universe. The reaction to anything Agatha related always remained the same. Violent, life threatening, way too much for Rio to handle.

 

(And she always ignored when anger and resentment shifted into lust and wonder. Rio tried to never acknowledge any piece of that)

 

Agatha had started teaching at the university a few years ago. Three achingly long years ago, to be exact. Not that Rio was counting. The newest professor was a quick hit. The talk of the campus barely into her first semester. After her first course, one class, just two hours and suddenly, every student wanted a piece of Professor Harkness. 

 

“Rhetoric: The Art of Persuasive Writing and Public Speaking”

 

Which should have been the only name, but after a month- Harkness and her students had given the title it’s own nickname, 

 

“That’s It! Now We’re Talking!” 

 

Rio silently scoffed, outwardly cringed. The name sounded straight out of some 80’s game show and after briefly meeting Agatha Harkness? That only made more sense as to why the name was chosen. 

 

The professor wasn’t like the rest. She wasn’t Jennifer Kale who was a woman full of sophistication. Who appeared to be above all, put together, and completely self centered. That last part, Rio had to learn to put up with. But, she was better than the Kaplan kid who didn’t know his left and rights. How he earned his role as a TA, she’d never know. But, that was Alice Wu-Gulliver’s issue to put up with. 

 

To make matters worse? Lilia Caldreu (The president of the university, or how she liked to be called as “ The Order of All Things”) was known to commonly take pity on the weak. Rio assumed that’s how a mess like Agatha Harkness was able to nudge her way in.​​ The only good thing the new addition had been good for was making Rio appreciate her time off more than ever. 

 

She’d always buried her head in work, never taking a breath or a second away from her classroom. (The others joked that the university was Rio’s home, second home, and vacation home all in one). 

 

But then, Agatha came along and suddenly, Rio felt a deep need. No- A strong desire to be a million miles away from the campus every chance given.

 

It wasn’t that Agatha was a bad person or a villain of the sorts, but she was in Rio’s eyes…weIl, immature. She didn’t seemingly take on the role as an educator as seriously as Rio did (in her mind, that was). Not to mention, Agatha couldn’t complete a sentence without a joke or insult. It drove Rio mad sitting in board meetings having to hear that grating, irritating, raspy, sexy voice (Okay, Rio was NOT supposed to think that, but she’d be lying to herself if she denied it).

 

For Rio, it had always been a dream since she was a little girl to become a botanist. The professor aspect came later on in life when her friend, Wanda Maximoff, mentioned how she’d rule a classroom with ease. Rio thought too how beautiful it’d be to inspire others, maybe lead them in the same career path she walked. Plus her love for plants, that was always a perk. 

 

To see someone as careless, reckless, spontaneous, unorganized as Agatha becoming the university’s favorite? Well, maybe Rio held a bit of jealousy. A slice of bitter resentment. 

 

And what didn’t help? Another reason the woman was everyone’s favorite? Something Rio found difficulty arguing or not understanding. 

 

“Did you see Professor Harkness today? She looks way too good in purple..”

 

“I swear, I need to get in that class”

“Oh shut up, you don’t even care about that subject. You just wanna stare at her”

“She’s hot!”

“Can’t blame you there..”

 

“Have you asked about her hair routine? I’m so jealous! I need it”

 

On and on, Rio would overhear students muttering amongst themselves. Not that she’d dare utter a word out loud, but..Rio agreed. How could she not? Agatha Harkness was a stunning human being from head to toe. She was tall, confident, strided with ease as if she ruled the universe. Her laugh was contagious, a smile that radiated through the halls. She had crystal blue eyes that Rio swore glimmered in the dull fluorescent lights. 

 

There’d be times during board meetings or in the break room, Rio found it difficult to not stare at the other professor. She’d try to hide her gaze, harden and disguise it as a glare. Agatha had only seemed to catch her once or twice (Rio never caught on to how it was much more than just a few times). Always a wiggle of her fingers, a wink followed along. Sometimes a dramatic mouthing of the words,

 

“Call me?” 

 

Which Rio always sneered at. She’d pack up her stuff, storm out of wherever they were to catch her breath.

 

Rio hated her. 

Rio couldn’t stand her. 

Rio wished Agatha Harkness never appeared in her life. 

 

No matter how hard she tried though? There was a tiny candle size flame burning within her. It never dulled, blew out into a cloud of smoke. The flame of intrigue and lust stayed bright, threatening to destroy her completely. 

 

She decided and told herself the feeling only developed out of spite. Maybe Rio held so much disgust for Agatha it turned into something else to prevent her from losing control. 

 

After all, Rio hadn’t been on a date let alone a hook up in years. Her head was buried in work, too distracted to have time for such things. So it only made sense seeing a woman such as Agatha striding through the halls, smirking everytime she caught Rio’s gaze, always irritating flirtatious comments that brought out something more than hatred within her- 

 

All of it made her feel something more than anger. It made sense it was nothing more than just being single for however many years. Hence why Rio was going on a date off an app her friend, Wanda, helped her create. 

 

Tinder. 

 

God, Rio felt pathetic for it. Luckily though the woman she was going to see was interesting and a treat for sore eyes. Eye candy, Wanda had wiggled her eyebrows while saying the name. Rio had rolled her eyes over that.

 

The date would help even if it led to a one night stand. Rio would be too in her head filled with disgust for herself over a hookup. Those always ruined her mentally, but…it’d distract her from Agatha. 

 

But for now? Just as always, Agatha skidded and danced her way around the rules. Which drove Rio to the verge of screaming every single time. Especially now unlike any other time before. 

 

“How the fuck did she manage to up and move her classroom overnight?” Rio asked with a shake of her head. “Did she fucking bribe Lilia into this?! That old woman has always been against creating chaos mid semester” 

 

“She’s Agatha,” Jen shrugged.

 

She’s Agatha. Fuck. That was always the explanation for how she managed to get away with things. 

 

“I don’t need to be three classrooms away from her,” Rio laughed, but it wasn’t humorous. No. It was complete disbelief filled with annoyance. “She’s loud enough and my classes need complete focus. Hearing her parties right down the hall won’t help”

 

“I know,” Jen agreed. “Go talk to Lilia about it. Maybe she’ll-”

 

“No,” Rio firmly said. “I’m not giving up my room. This has been my domain for years. Far longer than she’s even been here. Plus, all the natural lighting is perfect for the plants” 

 

She stood up from her chair, gesturing her hand in the air around to every plant scattered in her room. Jen watched as the woman began to pace, muttering incoherent Spanish under her tongue. A sign her blood was boiling with fury.

 

“No..” Rio shook her finger in the air, tossing her head side to side. 

 

“Noooo, what?” Jen asked. 

 

“She isn’t going to win” 

 

Jen chuckled. 

 

“Win what, exactly?”

 

“She doesn’t get to push me out, nope! Not a chance in hell, Jennifer!” 

 

“Oh, using my full name. Awesome” She rolled her eyes. “You better not take this out on me. I didn’-”

 

“She. Will. Not. Win!” 

 

The other woman muttered a low,

 

“Oh my god” 

 

Jen pushed herself off the desk, hands held up in surrender as she started to make her way to the door. 

 

“I need to go get ready for my next class. Good luck with…whatever this is- No, you know what?” Jen turned. “Focus on that date tonight, Rio. That’s more important don’t you think?” 

 

Rio stopped her pacing, sending a wide glare her way as she muttered, 

 

“I regret telling you about that..”

 

Jen laughed and tossed a wave over her shoulder, leaving her to her lonesome. However, that didn’t last more than two seconds. As if Rio’s temper couldn’t get any worse? 

 

“Howdy there!” 

 

The greeting chirped down the hall, Jen’s little laugh followed with some low chatter. No. That voice, it’s owner, fuck! Agatha was far too close to her room for her liking, gossiping with Jen most likely about god knows who. Maybe her, not that Rio cared (She did). 

 

“Go away..” Rio muttered under her breath as if Agatha would be able to hear her from afar. 

 

Her feet stormed over to the door, ready to slam it shut with dramatic force. She wanted to make a statement how Agatha was not welcome to be near her room more than she would be. The idea of seeing her in the hallway even more than before, hearing her voice clear as day. Not to mention that beautiful laugh that always was laced with the cutest snort- 

 

STOP!

 

Rio grabbed the edge of the door, ready to push it shut when the figure slithered before her. 

 

“Hey there neighbor” 

 

Fuck. She was too late. 

 

The older woman took in a deep breath, looking up to meet those sparkling blue eyes that shimmered with glee. It’s like she fed off being an annoyance, Rio swore it. 

 

“What do you want, Harkness?” Rio asked, voice monotone as if she was dead inside. 

 

“Just being courteous, giving my warm greetings to my new neighbors” 

 

She shrugged, holding out a tiny gift bag. It was a dark forest green, tied together with black ribbons and a purple bow on the side. Rio stared, trying to figure out what it was before she could open it. 

 

Did she even want to open it? No. She should shove it in Agatha’s face, add the reaction with a door slam and ignore her presence all together.  

 

Instead, her curiosity betrayed her when Agatha shook the bag in the air with a higher pitch,

 

“Made special for youuuu-”

 

Rio swiped it from her, not offering a warm grin or kind eyes. Her glare remained sharp. A frown stern stubborn to remain still. 

 

“Is that all?” She asked. 

 

Agatha shrugged again, both arms crossed against her chest as she leaned against the doorframe. 

 

“Nothing in return?”

 

“I didn’t know we were exchanging gifts. Let alone up and changing rooms” She snarled. “You know that’s ridiculous, right? You’re up and changing everything. Your students now have to change their routine and-”

 

“I needed a bigger room for my students,” Agatha explained. “Just as you need this,” She gestured into Rio’s spacious room. “For all your plants. Figured out of all of us, you’d understand”

 

Rio rolled her eyes, a tang of jealousy over how popular Agatha’s classes had become. Or…was it just jealousy that even more people had access to admire her all day? She voted the first (It was the second). 

 

“Great,” Rio said. “Again, is that it or would you like to continue being more annoying?”

 

“What would you prefer, Professor Vidal?” 

 

Agatha dropped her professional name every now and then. And when she did? She always laced it with the same silky tone, rich in a deep rasp while her head dipped lower. 

 

I hate you. 

 

“I think you know the answer” Rio nearly whispered, feeling the oxygen being stripped from her lungs. 

 

Agatha dramatically sighed, leaning back as she took a step away. 

 

“Well,” Agatha said. “Enjoy your weekend and the gift”

 

The woman slowly let that smug grin grow on her lips, wiggling her fingers in the air as she took a few steps back. In a small voice, one that sounded like it belonged to a ghost- She sang,

 

“Ta-ta” 

 

She then had the nerve to wink before spinning around, letting her heels click down the hall. Rio’s grip on the door tightened, knuckles turning a pale white as she tried to rip her eyes away from those hips. The ones that swayed rhythmically  back and forth. A movement that plunged Rio into a state of hypnosis.

 

“Professor Harkness!” 

 

The voice made Rio jump, eyes snapping over to Billy Kaplan running down the hall to meet her. 

 

“Don’t run. You’ll fall and smack your head again, kid” Agatha advised. 

 

He slowed down instantly just as anyone else would because as always, Agatha had a way with getting people to do whatever she said. Hell, Rio found herself falling under the same spell the others did at times. Whether it was handing her the copies out of the printer while she passed or even offering to hold the door open for her. 

 

Agatha was a witch and everyone knew it. Or, at least Rio knew.

 

As the two down the hall started to talk amongst themselves- Even from afar, Rio felt herself pulled into Agatha’s orbit. She was always such a strong presence even when her attention wasn’t on you. People always surrounded her, eager to hear what she said to say and hopeful she’d look their way. 

 

And once again? Her fucking beauty didn’t help.

 

Rio admired the white button up blouse with her sleeves rolled up. Purple slacks that captured her waist perfectly, but flowed loose at the same time. She stood tall with her heels that added a few extra inches. The wild hair that never seemed to know what a brush looked like drenched down to her mid back. Rio’s eyes trailed down, admiring each inch until-

 

Shit.

 

Agatha looked over as Billy searched through his bag. His lips were still moving at a fast pace, but Agatha didn’t seem to hear as she winked Rio’s way once again. Rio snapped out of her trance the second the wink registered in her mind. 

 

She shook her head, slamming the door shut and pressed her back against it with a strong inhale. Her eyes closed, trying to steady herself from the rush that coursed through her. 

 

I hate her. 

I hate her.

I hate her. 

 

Rio chanted the mantra, reminding herself of the truth (lie) to bring herself back down to earth. All was well after a few moments until she started to walk and felt the gift bag hit against her thigh. The reminder of Agatha’s gift was a punch, an annoying one more like. 

 

She paused, averting her eyes to the bag staring back at her almost as Agatha did so. Taunting, threatening, ready to drown her in regret at any given moment. 

 

Part of her wanted to just toss it in the trash and forget it existed. She had papers to grade, things to do. Agatha’s gift was below rock bottom on her list. 

 

Well…it should be. 

 

Rio placed it on her desk, staring and taking double glances its way. 

 

“No..” She muttered to herself.

 

The woman shook her head, storming away to rummage through her bag for a piece of gum. A way she had quit smoking a few months ago was by living off it. Especially in tense moments like so. Relief took over when the cinnamon flavor sprawled across her tongue, the rubber, chewy, texture softened between her teeth. 

 

However, when she turned back around to her desk- The small gift bag stripped any relief she had felt. Erasing its existence completely. Rio shook her head, muttering under her breath how ridiculous it was before storming back over. She didn’t waste another second. The sooner this bag was gone, sooner Agatha was out of her mind. 

 

Rio began to work quickly, pulling out the small amount of black tissue paper. What she wasn’t expecting was a needle point to nip her skin, bringing out a strong hiss followed by a muttered,

 

“What the fuck?!”

 

Agatha’s antics were now becoming violent. Awesome. Though, Rio briefly thought how that’d be a lovely way to get her fired. 

 

Though, to her surprise (and secret delight) the assailant was a simple tiny cactus, healthy as can be. 

 

“Well…hello there” Rio greeted with a soft smile as she did to any plant that was new to her. “Aren’t you a cute little thing?” 

 

She admired each inch of the small plant, smiling at its beauty. After a few seconds, her eyes drifted to the note attached against the plastic pot it was packed into. Her fingers unfolded it, eyes scanning the few words messy in Agatha’s scribbled writing,

 

“This plant is a prick. Suits you xo”

 

Pop. 

 

The bubble of Rio’s adoration and grin was tossed away. A bubble exploded into pieces of what it once was. 

 

She scoffed, crumbling the note and tossing it in the garbage with a low,

 

“Fucking Harkness”

 

The plant was cute, but really? Such a stupid insult. A joke that wasn't funny in the slightest. Whatever. Rio moved to take care of the plant, making it a home amongst the others. 

 

What Rio didn’t consider as she made the plant comfy in her room? Every single time her eyes caught a glimpse of the cactus, it’d spark Agatha in her mind more than she already dealt with. 

 

And maybe, just maybe, that was Agatha’s plan all along…

The freezers buzzed in Rio’s ear. Matched with the faint, crackling, radio above her. The speakers were clearly old and torn. Most definitely had seen better days. 

 

Suffering through them, A soft throwback station that played classics from the eighties. Cyndi Lauper, Michael Jackson, The Police, all the songs Rio knew like she knew her plants. Word for word, detail to detail. It was her favorite part of the grocery store as stupid as it sounded. 

 

But, it was different this time. She was fresh off a Tinder date that never happened. After sitting at a restaurant table on her own for over an hour as the staff gave her cringe worthy sympathetic looks- She just wanted to run and hide till the end of time. 

 

Typically, Rio would sing to each song under her breath. She loved doing so, drifting into her own little world even if she was in public. However, she couldn’t. Not after what just happened, where she was, and why she stood in the ice cream section of the store- Drenched in tears, heart aching as her mind dragged a big weight of despair. 

 

Nine PM. They were supposed to meet at nine for drinks and a late dinner. A Tinder date that Rio already thought was fucking stupid, but she’d be lying if she said there wasn’t some anticipation for it. The woman was nice, laidback. Their text conversations flowed with ease. Rio really thought meeting her, having a date, maybe it’d spark into something. A relationship of sorts that’d make her feel whole. 

 

Rio had been sitting in the corner booth, nursing a beer ever so slowly. Each time the door opened, her body perked up and she pulled out a warm smile. Though it was wasted when the glimpse of said person was not her Tinder date. Every ten minutes that passed turned into an hour, then another, and finally Rio had enough of embarrassing herself. 

 

She left cash on the table, far too much for a single beer and some pretzels. But, Rio didn’t care. The staff had been giving her way too many sympathetic stares and pathetic smiles to stay a second longer. She had texted the date letting her know she left, but by the time Rio pulled into the grocery store’s parking lot?

 

The woman must’ve unmatched them right after Rio messaged.

Everyone she knew had a significant other for the most part. It had been that way her entire life. She was nearing her forties and barely had three girlfriends. Wanda always tried to remind her it wasn’t a bad thing, but Rio hated it. 

 

When was it her turn to fall in love?

When would the universe send a woman her way to spend life with? 

 

Everyday, Rio felt she was running out of time. So much of her was preparing to grow old alone, digging her own grave in the most morbid way.

“Every step you take, I’ll be watching you…”

“Oh, can’t you see? You belong to me…”

 

If Rio was in a better mood, she’d look over and offer to add on another lyric with the woman. Maybe they’d laugh together, the moment would be sweet before both went their separate ways. However, that thought didn’t help. That should be her with another woman. Someone to fall in love with, dance in the grocery store close to midnight, make laugh and cherish time with. 

 

That’s all Rio wanted. Was it too much to ask for?

“This is my favorite one for the tears”

No. This can’t be real. This can not be possibly fucking real.

 

The universe hated her. Rio was certain because the universe wouldn’t give her a woman to fall in love with, no. But sure. It’d give her Agatha Harkness, the woman she couldn’t stand to be around. 

 

She shook her head, a puff of air pushed from her lungs as she took a step away to gather distance between them. Agatha was nearly shoulder to shoulder with her, gesturing to the freezer door with the pints of ice cream inside. Rio didn’t even know which flavor she was referring to, but she sure as shit wasn’t going to stick around to figure it out. 

 

Rio scoffed, muttering under her breath a few things in Spanish. From how ridiculous she was to cursing out the universe. 

 

“I’m just trying to be helpful, dear,” The woman sang (Or, was that Rio’s imagination because her voice was that damn nice?). “What’s got the tears rolling?” She questioned.

“Oh! Better yet, who has the tears roll-”

 

“Agatha,” Rio warned. 

 

“Was it my gift? Oh, you poor thin-”

 

Rio shook her head. Fuck. She wasn’t in the mood for this. 

 

“I said-”

 

“Yeah, yeah. I’m not deaf, you know?” Agatha laughed and that damn, cute, adorable, stupid fucking snort broke in between. “We aren’t at work, Professor . You don’t need to treat me as your rival-”

 

“You aren’t my rival,” Rio scoffed. 

 

You’re just my worst nightmare.

 

“A rival would mean there’s competition between us. There isn’t”

 

“Awe! So we are secret best friends?!” Agatha taunted.

 

Rio rolled her eyes, arms tightly crossed against her chest as she stormed off. She made sure their shoulders bumped into one another, making Agatha stumble back a bit as the woman let out a soft laugh followed by a call, 

 

“You forgot your ice cream!”

 

“Go to hell, Harkness!” Rio snapped back without a second thought. 

 

What the fuck, what the fuck?!

 

Her mind chanted the three words over and over. She was close to dropping the basket of snacks, running out of the store and maybe even put in her resignation from the university. 

 

Rio wasn’t sure what was worse anymore. Was it being stood up? Or how the universe never letting her meet a woman to fall in love with? And now, the most annoying co-worker who taunted and teased the hell out of her found her sobbing in the ice cream section on a Friday night. 

 

The third. That had to be the worst thing the universe had ever gifted her. 

 

The woman slipped back into the chip aisle, catching her breath right next to the Doritos. She kept a hand over her stomach, telling herself it was just the emotions and she was not going to toss up the beer and pretzels from before. That’d only sign her death certificate if she were to vomit all over the tile floor for Agatha to inevitably see. 

 

About two minutes had gone by when Rio finally felt her lungs find a steady pace. She wiped her eyes again, feeling the craving for ice cream strengthen more than before. The frozen dessert was always her go to as emotional support. 

 

She’s gone. No doubt about it. Rio told herself. 

 

And the same thing she said earlier to Jennifer about her classroom?

 

She does not get to win. 

 

Rio held her head up high, stomping back to the ice cream section- Agatha Harkness be damned. She wasn’t going to derail her from comfort food. She already saw her covered in tears, drenched in sorrow and despair. Wasn’t that the worst of it all already?

Shit. 

You’ve gotta’ be kidding me…

 

When Rio turned the corner, she found Agatha standing in the middle of the aisle. Her pint of ice cream in her hand, looking down at the floor like she was checking if her feet were trapped in cement blocks. Rio noticed how it was the exact same spot she left her in. Unmoved, untouched. A statue or a robot who ran out of battery power. 

 

The other brunette hadn’t looked up at her. Rio still had a window to escape and try desperately to forget this encounter ever happened.

 

No. She isn’t going to win.

 

Rio cleared her throat, taking fast steps to the freezer as she rasped out a quick,

 

“Is letting unpurchased ice cream melt a hobby of yours?”

“Come over to my place and find out” She winked. 

 

Why is she like this?
