“And please remember, no exceptions or excuses for tardiness over the next few classes! My door will not be locked, but you will get a mark taken off your grade”

 

Muttered words and hushed groans echoed through the room. Rio scoffed as she added an amused,

 

“I know! How dare I care about you getting your or better yet, your parents- money's worth of learning..” 

 

A few students chuckled as they gave Rio a soft goodbye while the others stormed out with no word to offer. She forced a small grin, waved to the students who adored her more than the rest, but once the classroom door shut and Rio was left the last man standing?

 

She exhaled a long breath, dropping in her desk chair with hands pressed over her face. 

 

Fuck. 

 

It had been a long week. A painful five days that felt never ending. That feeling was foreign to her. Rio loved her job and at times, the semester felt like two seconds leaving her to wish for more. 

 

However, this time around? The weekend couldn’t come soon enough. 

 

Monday morning had been the start of the worst week of her life. Five days had gone by achingly slow. Her entire routine was tossed out the window. 

 

It all started with walking to her classroom Monday morning, her usual routine of being on the phone with Wanda before they went on with their busy day. They would discuss their plans, make a date for drinks for Friday night. That part of her routine was there like clockwork. 

 

However, what was missing? Better yet, who was missing?

 

Fucking Harkness..

 

Typically Agatha would tease her from behind in the parking lot (They always arrived at the same time on Mondays. The only day Agatha wasn’t running late) while Rio would be on the phone, hearing Agatha mimic her words. 

 

“Yeah, yeah..I know,” Rio sighed. “I’m just- Do we have to go for drinks? Why can’t we just bury ourselves on my couch or yours?”

 

Wanda scoffed, but Rio didn’t hear her response. Instead her ears focused into the voice behind her. 

 

“Oh! How can I possibly leave my plants alone?!” Agatha faked a southern accent (Rio was never sure why that was the common one she used, but whatever). “They must be accompanied at all times. Good golly, I’d say they’re a society of my very own!”

 

“Jesus, hang on-” Rio muttered before spinning around. “The sun has barely risen and you’re already on my nerves-”

 

“Aren’t I always, sugar?” Agatha smirked. 

 

Rio grunted, storming off as she muttered how annoying she was under her breath. 

 

She had grown accustomed to the unbearable woman on her tail. The sudden absence, disturbance in routine left Rio looking over her shoulder, waiting for Agatha to jump out from behind a corner or out of thin air. But alas, she had been left with the same thing. 

 

Nothing.

 

No sound.

 

Not a peep. 

 

Just an empty space behind her. 

 

Maybe Agatha was late, that was common. She always ran behind schedule. Her students were more prepared than she ever would be. But as the days progressed, Rio noticed a shift in Agatha’s dynamic with her. 

 

She wouldn’t offer a teasing grin. No fingers wiggled in the air with an exaggerated mouthed, 

 

“Call me” 

 

If Rio happened to see her in the hallway, Agatha would quickly shield herself or dodge her before their eyes were even able to connect. Rio almost felt as if she was a nuisance and their dynamic became the reverse. 

 

This is what you’ve always wanted. 

 

Rio told herself those words on repeat. She tried to think about how she didn't have to endure Agatha’s antics, be chased from the parking lot to her classroom, feel those piercing blue eyes watching her every move. 

 

Agatha was leaving Rio the hell alone like she had told her to do for three years now. 

 

This is what you’ve always wanted. 

 

Not to mention, Rio’s other command had been followed like an order. A strict obligation for the past weekend to even happen. 

 

This weekend never happened. 

And just as she demanded, the weekend seemingly ceased to exist. It was almost as if Agatha and her had made a pact to never acknowledge the other again. 

 

Isn’t that even more than you asked for?

 

A few knocks on her classroom door snapped her back awake. She hadn’t fallen asleep, only sunk into the pit of despair over anything else. A daze that only involved Agatha Harkness. Which wasn’t a shocker with how often Rio had drifted off to that place in her mind. The corner tucked in the back, cobwebs and darkness eliminated. Now a shining bright light with just a lone stool, a photo of Agatha beside it. 


Rio shook her hands to rid the jitters, rolling her neck as she pushed herself up, shuffling around the desks-

 

Maybe it’s her.

 

The three words punched her in the chest. Her hopes skyrocketed, she felt her heart kick into gear, hands made work to straighten her outfit- A black button up top, slim pair of black slacks. Nothing fancy and if it was Agatha at the door- Suddenly Rio wished she dressed better. 

 

What? Stop caring how you look for her, idiot. 

 

She mentally groaned, hating herself more than she had in years. With a deep breath, trembling hands, Rio opened the door to find-

 

“Afternoon, freak” Alice smiled. 

 

Dammit. 

 

“Hey,” Rio sighed, leaning against the doorframe as she forced a small smile herself. “Heading out early?” She gestured to the bag on Alice’s shoulder.

 

“Yeah, cancelled my last class”

 

“Playing hooky with Kale again?” Rio smirked a bit. 

 

She watched the woman’s cheeks begin to burn. How her eyes sparkled, looking away while her foot kicked at the floor. Rio laughed, amused by the little girl crush her friend wore. 

 

If only my crush was that easy- Not a crush. Stop it. 

 

“It’s cute,” Rio shrugged. “Odd duo, stuck up bitch, but..cute” 

 

Alice scoffed. 

 

“She’s not that bad”

 

“You’re only saying that because you’re going down on her…or the reverse? You know what,” Rio put her finger up, scrunching her nose as she shook her head. “I don’t want to know” 

 

They both chuckled, but were cut off as Billy (William? Rio never knew which name that boy went by) flew by with two coffees in his hands. His breath was short, rapid as his shoulders raised up and down. He gave a little smile, nodding to them both before asking,

 

“Hey, have you guys seen-”

 

“They’re in the library” 

 

Alice finished for him, knowing exactly who he was looking for and also? She did not want Rio to catch on for who he was looking for and why he was searching for them. 

 

“Great, thank you” He sighed. 

 

Going against Alice’s hopes to swiftly push him away, distract and get Rio to walk out with her early. The young man crushed her attempt with unintentional ease.

 

“I swear, Agatha’s coffee days will be the death of me” 

 

Shit. 

 

“Oh, coffee Friday?” Rio perked up. 

 

“Mhm” He smiled. “You know how it is” 

 

She smirked a bit. 

 

“Yeah, I-”

 

“Might want to catch them before they fly off,” Alice weakly smiled. 

 

He nodded, saying a quick goodbye to them both before rushing down the hall. 

 

After being ignored by Agatha for the last five days, drowning in the memories of the weekend- Rio (unfortunately) was excited to hear Agatha was doing her monthly coffee run. Where she picked a random Friday and bought coffee for everyone. 

 

(Well, everyone meaning the staff in their department…more so, just the few people Agatha tolerated)

 

Of course, Rio never pitched in by giving William her order. However, that didn’t leave her with nothing. 

 

Agatha would always decide for her. Hence why part of her was excited. She loved seeing what the annoying woman came up with, but even worse? Now, it was a way to connect herself to Agatha. 

 

The woman's absence felt hollowing the last few days. Rio was eager to let a small coffee cup designed by her help her with it. 

 

Oh, what am I becoming? Rio wondered. 

 

“Assuming mine is left in the break room per normal?” She asked. 

 

Though as Alice’s smile faded, looking elsewhere while she hid behind her coffee-

 

“What’s that face for?” Rio asked. 

 

Alice shrugged, running a hand through her hair while avoiding Rio’s stare.

 

“Uh..well, that’s the thing-” She nervously laughed before quickly mumbling the words, “All the coffees have been.. given ”

 

“Okay? Where’s mine?” Rio questioned, but realized the answer not a second later. “Wow-” 

 

“She didn’t say anything to me!” Alice put her hands up in defense. “All I know is there’s no other-”

 

“Yeah! K’, cool…got it. Thanks!”  

 

Rio disappeared into her classroom, slamming the door shut behind her. 

 

Agatha was ignoring her, disappearing left and right and now wouldn’t even include Rio for a stupid coffee? What the fuck?! She excluded her, made her the odd one out. While everyone strided around with their large cup of coffee, wearing smiles and laughter from the joy a simple drink could bring- Rio stood with nothing.

 

Fucking bitch..

 

Sure, this is what Rio had always wanted. But after their weekend together? How things felt completely different off campus with just one another around? She’d be lying if she said this is exactly what she had truly desired. If anything, the more time that passed left Rio to realize this was the polar opposite. 

 

All she had to do was laugh Agatha off, storm out of that store and never look back. Agatha would still be teasing her, annoying her and the best of all?

 

I’d never know what could be..what we could be..

 

Rio rushed to grab her belongings, desperate to get home and bask in the glory of her liquor cabinet or maybe a few beers. Rio would know which vice she needed when her pajamas were on, a shitty movie was on the screen, and reality truly struck her for the mess she had created. 

 

She looked around, making sure everything was in her hands. With a few heavy breaths, the classroom door locked behind her- Rio turned to see two staff members laughing with the coffee cups in their hands. She curled her lips in a snarl, scrunched her nose in disgust, muttering under her breath, 

 

“Fuck off, Harkness..”

Rio used her shoulder to push the door open, stepping into the parking lot as she texted Wanda back about meeting for drinks. As much as she didn’t want to go out, getting drunk with others was a better idea over drinking alone. Sometimes she was smart. 

 

Key word, sometimes. 

 

“Shit!” 

 

Rio’s head snapped up from her phone when the word was shouted. She searched across the lot for the voice’s owner, scanning each row until-

 

Agatha. 

 

The woman was crouched down on the cement, picking up the items that had flown out of her bag. Rio’s heart thundered, alarms in her mind going off with a warning to flee the scene. The petty side of her wanted to do just as Agatha had been. Ignore, dodge, turn a blind eye and not offer her anything. 

 

Unfortunately, that wasn’t in Rio’s nature. Even if they were still enemies (More than they seemingly were now) she’d help her pick the mess up. 

 

Rio slipped her phone in her pocket, jogging over before her knees nearly scraped across the cement just as Agatha’s belongings had. Her hands worked to pick up the miscellaneous items. A deck of playing cards, mascara, a pack of gum and a tiny baggy of cinnamon discs. 

 

This is so Agatha.. Rio tried to not grin as she thought it over. 

 

She didn’t notice how the woman beside her jumped, froze, her own anxiety screaming inside. Rio was too busy picking up the other items, handing them to Agatha with a small smile. One that was nervous, careful to not scare her off. 

 

However, Agatha never looked up at her. There was no smile in return, no witty comment about Rio being her savior or something like so. 

 

Agatha stood back on her feet with ease. She tucked her purse back together, straightening her clothes and never turning her attention to the woman stunned below. All she offered was a low, clipped, barely coherent, 

 

“Thanks..” 

 

Before turning around, storming off and leaving stunned behind. 

 

Seriously?

 

She scoffed, shaking her head as she muttered a snarky reply to the one worded graciousness Agatha had given her. 

 

“Yeah, don’t be too enthusiastic over it or anything..” 

 

Rio had started to walk away, missing how Agatha spun around the second she had opened her mouth. All she heard was the sarcastic wit, attitude coating her tone,

 

“Oh! Silly me! I’m just jumping for joy for how I almost just broke my phone and all my shit went flying across the parking lot. Hip-hip- fucking- horray!”  

 

Rio turned back around, being met with a harsh glare that Agatha never showed. Sure, they glared at one another. But, it wasn’t the ice cold icicle being stabbed through her right then. 

 

Who knew I’d miss her playful glare so much?

 

Standing in the university’s parking lot on a late Friday afternoon, Rio was learning how Agatha couldn’t hide annoyance and anger to save her life. That was for sure. 

 

“Jeez. Sorry I helped, I guess” Rio said. 

 

Agatha scoffed. 

 

“Oh, cry me a river, Vidal!”

 

“What is up your ass?!” Rio asked. “You’re acting as if I am the worst human being by helping pick your mess up!”

 

Agatha laughed with no humor. Only malicious intent and rage filled its tone. 

 

“Whatever” Rio muttered, shaking her head as she went to turn around. “Go back to acting as if I don’t exist”

 

Agatha’s laughter stopped, lips curled up slowly as she snarled back, 

 

“Monday morning, back to usual. Act like that weekend never happened. Sound familiar?” 

 

Rio swallowed, taking a step back in case she needed to run. Not from the truth or how right Agatha was. This was her own fault and Rio knew it. 

 

More so she’d be running because fuck, Agatha’s anger was terrifying. 

 

She looked on the verge of lunging out, strangling Rio’s throat- Not the way she had dreamt about either. Everyone knew Agatha was a powerful being, someone who was a force to be reckoned with, but..this was different. Terrifyingly different. 

 

Rio shook her head, voice starting to waver with every word,

 

“This is different. Not usua-”

 

“How so?” Agatha questioned, arms folded against her chest as her foot began to tap. “Hm? I’m doing exactly as you wanted and more! You’ve told me for years to leave you alone. I’d say I’m giving you the entire package!”

 

Rio shook her head. 

 

“That’s not fair”

 

It is fair. 

 

“You're acting as if I don't exist. After the weekend, I-”

 

“The weekend never happened! You said it yourself multiple times!” She exclaimed. “God!” Agatha scoffed, looking away with her hand running through her hair. “I can’t do anything right when it comes to you” 

 

Rio opened her lips to say something, but the words were vacant. They vanished into thin air, being replaced with a silence that spoke louder than her voice ever could. She felt like a dam had been built in front of her, impossible to break through and let the flood drown Agatha out. 

 

“Yeah..” Agatha scoffed. “Exactly. So, goodbye Rio” 

 

She watched as Agatha turned, making her way back to the car that Rio hated she missed. Rio was frozen, her heart begging to stop her while every other piece of her told her to turn around, give it up. 

 

Rio did this. She had created the damage between them by begging, pleading for years the woman left her alone. Her wish was true, the genie in a bottle granted her that. 

 

So why the hell was she pissed off watching Agatha walk away? 

Why did Rio care that Agatha didn’t want anything to do with her? 

 

Well…to be fair-

 

“You started this”

 

The three childish words escaped before Rio was able to catch them. On one half, she was lucky for how they were successful by making Agatha stop in her tracks. The other though? 

 

Oh, I’m dead..

 

Agatha started to take dangerously slow steps, head tilted as her eyes narrowed in as if Rio was her prey. She was circling, pointing, ready to attack and kill her with one swing.

“What are you talking about, Rio?” 

 

Her voice was low, daring Rio to argue and worst of all? 

 

Jesus. The way she says my name is so stupidly attractive. Fucking hell..

 

Rio cleared her throat, standing up taller, a hand gesturing out with every word,

 

“Years ago the night we met. You were an ass-”

 

“And I’ve spent three years trying to make that wrong a right!” 

 

Agatha yelled, the veins in her neck sticking out stronger with every word. Rio jumped in her spot, leaning back as Agatha started to charge toward her. No more dangerous slow steps, a full on run Rio should move from. Turn around, run away before she’d be slaughtered to death in the university’s parking lot. 

 

But instead, Rio stayed put. She braced herself for the impact, but couldn’t prepare for the way her stomach swirled as Agatha was just a shy four steps away. Close enough to feel her presence stronger than crouched down beside her. She leaned back, fists scrunched into balls while her heart pounded like a bass drum.

 

Agatha’s vanilla conditioner was strong, the smell of coffee still lingered on her lips and those piercing blue eyes looked frozen. 

 

“I know!” She tossed her arms out. “I’m so wicked and evil for how I read the situation wrong! Damn me to hell for eternity-”

 

“Agatha-”

 

“I thought you’d be one into a bit of competitive flirting, my fucking bad for being wrong. I didn’t realize you’d punish me for years over that. Hell, if I did- We would have never talked!” 

 

“Yeah?! Well maybe that’s how it should’ve stayed!” 

 

Rio yelled, pushing forward so their faces were inches away, but that didn’t last long. 

 

Just as quick as they were close to touching, silently debating attacking the other in a brutal kiss to end whatever this feud was. They leaned away from one another in sync. 

 

Both of their faces filled with rage shifted into something unreadable to one another. Rio swallowed the lump in her throat, watching as Agatha ripped her eyes away. Before she did so, Rio saw the water melting the frozen blue orbs that had lost all strength. She didn’t miss how Agatha visibly trembled, lifting her head to speak, but instead just stormed off quicker than before. 

 

And suddenly, Rio preferred Agatha’s life threatening anger over the back of her body as she ran off.

 

She stayed in her spot, unable to move while staring into the void space Agatha left. Down the parking lot the car door slammed shut, flying off as soon as the engine was turned on. Agatha was there and she was gone in what felt like less than thirty seconds. 

 

Rio sucked her cheeks in, holding arms over her stomach while no other thoughts were in her mind. Only the hollowing question, 

 

What just happened?

Rio sprawled every limb over the couch, draping herself as if she were a blanket. A half empty tub of rocky road ice cream tucked in her side, whiskey bottle on the floor in arms reach, with a crappy reality TV show she was definitely not paying attention to. 

 

She wasn’t sure how long it had been since she had trudged through her front door. The only few things she focused on was letting Nicky outside and making sure he was fed. Kicking her shoes off, grabbing a bottle of whiskey and ice cream (A perfect dinner. Gordon Ramsey would most certainly be proud) and collapsing with a thud onto the couch.

 

Everything else was background, nothing mattered nor did she have the energy for it all. The fight with Agatha lived in her mind as a being separate from her own self. She couldn’t control the memory. It carried its own heart, pulse, thoughts and life. If Rio could gain control, she would’ve by now. 

 

To be fair, the whiskey most likely wasn’t helping the memory’s existence die. 

 

“Oh, what the fuck” 

 

Rio jumped, but never bothered to sit up. Her head shot over to the redhead standing above her. The woman’s eyes roaming her up and down, scanning around the room with Nicky sniffing her up and down. She slowly started to laugh, holding her hands up with a shake of her head. 

 

“Nuh-uh, nope!” She laughed, reaching for the TV remote to turn the show off. “There’s no way one Tinder date gone wrong is going to do this to you”


“What the hell?” Rio whined. “Where did you come from?! Ever heard of knocking-”

 

“Ever heard of cancelling plans? Maybe answering your phone so I know you aren’t dead?” She countered, arms folded tight against her chest. 

 

“I-”

 

Wanda reached down, snatching her phone off the coffee table and scoffed at the black screen facing her. 

 

“Course,” She scoffed, holding it up for Rio to see. “Why charge the device that lets me know you’re alive?” 


Rio shrugged. “More fun that way”

 

“Yeah, so is letting me know you’re staying home” She said, rolling her eyes. “Especially when you’re..” She waved her hand up and down. “What is this, exactly?”

 

“You barging into my house, that’s what this is..” Rio grumbled. 

 

Wanda let out a laugh, tossing her head back as she held her hands up theatrically. 

 

“Okay, sure- That’s the answer!” She exclaimed. “Not the fact you’ve obviously been sobbing your eyes out, not even in your pajamas, a bottle of whiskey and to top it all off?!”

 

She leaned down, ripping the ice cream container from her hold. Her eyes squinted, nose scrunched as she realized-

 

“Liquid ice cream” Wanda said, returning her eyes back to Rio. “But, you’re so right. Nothing else is the issue here” 

 

Wanda smirked as Rio’s demeanor sunk back into herself. She twiddled with her thumbs, pulled her bottom lip back between her teeth with a small shrug. 

 

“Maybe I like my ice cream liquid-y now. Ever consider that?” She mumbled.

 

“Oh,” Wanda nodded, clicking her tongue with a wink. “Makes sense. You also love sulking in your work clothes while crying and drinking whiskey. Man, this new Rio era is really not a problem at all”

 

“Exactly!” Rio said, holding her hand in the air. “Now, give me back my liquid dessert and head for the door-”

 

“No and no,” Wanda declined. “I am going to plug your phone in, put this soup of yours away and you-” 

 

She pointed, finding the box of tissues to toss at her. 

 

“You’re going to sit up, use a few of these and when I get back- Tell me what the hell is going on” 

 

Wanda was exiting the room, but not without swiping the whiskey bottle Rio had taken a hold of out of her hand. 

 

Rio groaned, throwing her head back with a whine. “I hate you!” 

 

“I know you do!” Wanda called back. 

 

She listened to the woman putting away her two favorite vices, plugging her phone in and most definitely getting herself a bottle of wine. Rio didn’t blame her there. If she found Wanda in this state, she’d need an entire liter of vodka to make it through. 

 

Rio forced herself to sit up before Wanda would do it for her. She tucked her knees up to her chest, Nicky jumping up to snuggle in beside her. 

 

“I guess you’re better than snuggling liquid ice cream..” Rio murmured, leaning down to kiss the top of his head. 

 

Wanda snickered as she strided back into the room. 

“I’d argue much better, but..” She dropped the water bottle in her lap, dropping on the other end of the couch beside her. “To each their own” 

 

The silence remained for a minute or so. Wanda allowed Rio to blow her nose, wipe the remaining tears and take a few sips of her water. She gave her time to collect herself the best she could, letting her study close and try to pick apart what (Better yet, who) created this version of her best friend. 

 

Wanda stared…and stared- Rio side glancing every few seconds until she shifted uncomfortably in her spot. 

 

“I think she’s judging us..” Rio mumbled against Nicky's head, hiding her face behind him. 

 

The redhead smirked, taking a sip from her wine before exhaling a sigh. 

 

“Not judging, simply…reading-”

 

“Judging” 

 

“Investigating” 

 

“You aren’t on the payroll for such a thing” Rio rolled her eyes. 

 

“I work for a nonprofit,” Wanda shrugged. 

 

“Oh yeah? What’s your organization called? Far Too Nosy Redheads?”

 

“Hmm,” Wanda hummed, pretending to think about it. “We debated that title for awhile, but ended up going with a third party recommendation” 

 

Rio chuckled. “Oh really? And what was the recommendation?” 

 

“You Can’t Keep Distracting the Redhead Nonprofit Investigator Society”  

 

Rio’s smirk faded, eyes lowered back to the boy snuggled in her side. She heard Wanda humming her successful tune. The one that sang, “I won” their back and forth. 

 

“Society? That makes you sound like the leader of some cult..” She muttered. 

 

“Well then, you should feel honored you’re my first vulnerable soul to be corrupted” Wanda replied. 

 

The amusement in Wanda’s voice was cut, tone short, not letting Rio prolong their conversation any longer. 

 

“Now. Out with it. What’s the pity party about?” She asked. 

 

Rio looked up before back down. She shifted her body left to right, clearing her throat as her fuzzy drunken mind tried to scramble an excuse together. All the words felt jumbled, coherent thoughts non existent. One vision stayed clear in her mind, a look that only made her stomach feel sicker than the whiskey ever could. 

 

“What is going on in there?” Wanda asked. “I’m not even in your brain and I feel sick-”

 

“Is that an insult?” 

 

“Just an observation” 

 

She shrugged, taking a slow sip from her wine, allowing Rio a few more seconds to reply. But when she didn’t, Wanda simply sighed, her heart breaking for whatever happened to her best friend. 

 

Rio had rarely looked so destroyed in her life. Only when her father passed could it compare. And as heavy as that weighed, the destruction it had caused- Wanda would be a liar if she said this didn’t feel different. She was dressed in remorse, covered in despair, wreaked of guilt like never before. 

 

Rio, what the hell did you do?

 

“I won’t let you dodge my ques-”

 

“That stupid Tinder date” Rio lied and shit- That even sounded pathetic to her. “It..y’know, got ghosted and-”

 

“You were over the moon having an excuse to delete Tinder” Wanda pointed out. “That’s not it, you’re a horrible liar and we both know it”

 

“Wow..” Rio puffed out a hint of a laugh. “You’re just lovely company to have, aren’t you?”

 

She looked up to find Wanda smiling big, holding her wine glass in the air with a tiny bow, an arm extended out to her side. 

 

“What can I say? I’m just a gem”

 

“A gem that’s a pain in my ass” 

 

“What about a rose thorn in your side? Sounds prettier” 

 

“Nope” Rio popped the p, shaking her head. “You’re too aggravating to be a peaceful pain” She shrugged. “Up my ass hurts worse”

 

“Not a fan of ana-”

 

Rio groaned, grabbing a pillow to hold over her face, voice muffled as she yelled,

 

“Ew! Ugh, fuck off. Go home. Leave me be!” 


Wanda laughed as she choked on the red liquid that felt perfect on her tongue, delicious to sweeten this bitter moment. Well…maybe bitter was a bit too harsh. Making Rio cringe through her apparent breakdown was humorous, after all. 

 

“I will do such a thing when you admit to what’s going on!” She exclaimed.  

 

Rio grumbled under her breath. A variety of words that all added up to the same result,

 

“This is so stupid”

 

Typically, Wanda would continue arguing until Rio either gave up the answer in a rage or turned into a puddle on the floor. Luckily for her though, she could tell Rio was reaching her breaking point. 

 

It showed how she was fidgeting with Nicky’s ear, her tongue swiping the inside of her cheek every now and then, lips pulled back, fingers tapping rhythmically against her knee. 

 

“Agatha got coffee for everyone”

 

Wanda had been taking a small sip of wine, thinking she had more time before Rio confessed. Though as the wine glass sat against her lips, studying Rio to see if this was one of her annoying jokes. Where she’d say anything to dodge the actual question, the real conversation, to avoid the truth all together. 

 

She isn’t joking..?

 

The woman swallowed, clearing her throat before asking,

 

“So..why uh- You care she bought coffee for everyone? I thought you hated when she-”

 

“Everyone but me!” Rio yelled through a strong laugh. “Everyone else in that damn building got a coffee!”

 

Okay, building was an exaggeration. BUT! Still! Rio was the only staff member who didn’t have a coffee purchased by Agatha in her hand. That earned her the right to react this way. 

 

Anyone else who had been left out for coffee day would react the same way… right?  

 

“And what do I get?! I get that bitch having the audacity to fight me in the parking lot- AFTER PICKING UP HER THINGS!” 

 

Wanda was a deer in headlights. A confused deer to be exact and that was probably still too light of a word for it. She felt frozen, eyes wide as she watched the meltdown happen live in action. Rio’s voice was cracking, hands waving in the air as her words screamed out. Her eyes only drifted to see the dog burying himself deeper in Rio’s side, thinking softly to herself, 

 

Poor Nicky. You’re such a trooper. 

 

“She’s such a bitch Wanda, I-”

 

“Okay, okay” Wanda held her hand up, chuckling softly. “Slow down for one, how much did you have to drink? I’m so confus-”

 

Rio continued, but not with the answers Wanda was exactly looking for. 

 

“And I didn’t know telling her to forget the weekend would mean this!” She yelled, balling up her fist as she shook her head. “If I did, I-”

 

“Honey, you gotta’ guide me here. I’m lost” She chuckled. 

 

As if Wanda’s voice wasn’t gentle, almost like Rio was at the interrogation table with a lightbulb shining on her- She broke under the heated pressure. 

 

Rio’s head shook, she made Nicky jump off the couch when she screamed the words that the neighbours were sure to hear. 

 

“We hung out! Okay?!” 

 

Wanda watched as her best friend was trembling physically and vocally. She was picking at her fingernails, shaking her head as if she was trying to ruin her brain. Every little action Wanda analyzed, the words that pieced the woman’s current state together-

 

Oh my god. 

 

She brought the wine glass up to her lips, tipping back with one swig while wishing it was the entire bottle. Truthfully, Wanda would need an entire case if the direction they were going in was to the destination she already knew. 

 

Rio had her heart broken a few years ago. It was the last time she really opened herself to date anyone. After that, Rio shut down straight into ultra work mode. Natasha and Wanda tried everything to get her out of it, but no dice. Tinder was a massive breakthrough, but that had failed and they couldn’t put up an argument over it. Rio was stood up, that was enough to allow the app to be gone. 

 

And yet during all of their scheming, plotting, brainstorming on how to get their friend back out there-

 

Agatha Harkness.

 

The name was never hated by Wanda. She remembered three years ago when Rio said those two words, gave her the rundown of their first encounter- Wanda went home that night to Natasha with the words, 

 

“There’s something about that name” 

 

Natasha looked up from her phone with a small smirk. 

 

“Agatha sounds like it belongs to an old woman? Is that i-”

 

“Shut up” Wanda sighed, playfully smacking her shoulder. “Listen to me!” 

 

“Okay, okay” Natasha put her phone down, hands up in surrender. “You have my undivided attention, honey”

 

Wanda rolled her eyes, crashing on the couch beside her. She shook her head, biting at her bottom lip as the name echoed off every wall in her mind. 

 

There was something about the way Rio said her name. Their first encounter as well may have been a subtle amount of flirting before it crashed. She didn’t think that was it. Even if Rio said they didn’t flirt or never even spoke, Wanda would be feeling something in her gut. 


“You’re usually right about these things..” Natasha said. “So..what’s the name telling you”

 

Wanda scoffed. “You’re gonna’ laugh”

 

“Try me,” Natasha said.

 

She tugged her lips back between her teeth, nibbling until letting them loose to explain. 

 

“She’s the one..” Wanda shrugged. “I- I don’t know how else to explain it besides…the way Rio said it, even if she’s annoyed by her and all like-”

 

Natasha didn’t say anything, knowing well to let the silence linger, give her space to continue on when she was ready 

 

“Rio and Agatha. Agatha and Rio. Rio Vidal, Agatha Harkness- It works” 

 

“Hm..” Natasha hummed. “She’s stubborn, you have to keep that in mind. Don’t get your hopes up”

 

Wanda had been trying for months to push her best friend back out there, eager to see her fall in love like she deserved. Natasha had been supportive, helpful, but still kept her grounded before she could truly get her hopes out of hand. 

 

“I just want to see her happy. Am I too obsessive about this?” She looked over to find Natasha giving a small smile. “Am I?” She repeated. 

 

Natasha shook her head. “You’re a good friend”

 

“Well..mark my words. This is it”

 

“I believe you,” She nodded. “Guess we’ll see how it plays out”

 

“You know, I said awhile ago Rio was destined for an enemies to lovers plot”

 

The other woman laughed, tucking a piece of red hair behind Wanda’s ear. 

 

“I can see it”

 

“Right?!” Wanda grinned. “It makes so much sense!” 

 

Rio groaned, hands covering her face as she dug the heel of her palms into her cheeks. 

 

“She bought my stupid ice cream and snacks” 

 

She began and oh lord, Wanda would never guess where the confession was heading. 

 

“We spoke for hours and then we went to a rage room- Which my shoulder is still sore from and that was all because I accidentally liked her stupid Instagram post and this-”

 

Rio hiccuped, struggling to take a breath through a few tiny coughs. Wanda went into action, putting her wine glass down to exchange it for the water bottle. She twisted the cap, holding it to her with a soft, 

 

“Hey, hey..” Wanda said. “Drink some water, catch your breath” 

 

Reluctantly, Rio took the water from her. She took a few sips, caught her breath and wiped tears before they could reach her cheeks. The woman shook her head, muttering under her breath,

 

“I hate her so much..” Rio lied. 

 

Wanda snickered. 

 

“I don’t think you would be here a drunken mess if that were the case..”

 

Rio shrugged. 

 

“Who knows? Maybe this is-”

 

“Don’t do that” Wanda said, the softness in her voice gone as if it was never there. “Listen, I won’t press you harder tonight for information about…how the hell you two hung out-”

 

“Good. I’m too tired”

 

Wanda gave a soft smile. 

 

“Too drunk as well”

 

“I’m not that-”

 

“Rio, honey you’re slurring every other word..” Wanda said. “Besides, I know you. Let’s just..watch something on TV. If you want to talk, I’m all ears”

 

She reached forward for the remote, grabbing the fleece blanket to lay over their legs. Rio wouldn’t say it, too lost in her emotions, but…she was thankful for Wanda beyond words. 

 

When Rio ended up in this state of mind, it was hard to talk about anything. Especially making sense through each word. Not to mention, she had just confessed to hanging out with her worst enemy of all time. Part of her knew when she was good and sober, Wanda would most likely recruit Natasha to gang up on her. 

 

Wait-

 

“You’re just waiting for Natasha to be back in town to interrogate me..huh?”

 

Natasha was away for work for the weekend, due to come home the following week. Rio wasn’t surprised when Wanda snickered, leaning back as she scrolled through Netflix’s wide selection. 

 

“I hate the both of you..” Rio grumbled. 

 

“More than Agatha Harkness now, apparently” Wanda replied. 

 

“No. I still really hate her” Rio lied. 

 

“Mhm. Okay, Rio” 

 

“I do!” 

 

“I’m not saying you don’t!” 

 

“I hate her”

 

“Yep. Keep drinking water, drunkie” 

 

Wanda popped the p, not letting the argument go on as she selected Grace and Frankie to watch for the millionth time together. Rio did as she told her, slumping in her spot more as the theme song started to roll. Normally they’d sing it horribly together, but Rio was too busy thinking to herself-

 

I still hate her…don’t I?

The following night rolled around far too soon for Rio’s liking. Saturday night, one day closer to Monday when she’d have to face Agatha all over again. Plus, another day closer to when Natasha and Wanda were certain to break her door down. 

 

They’d be around for dinner Thursday night with relentless questions about what happened. It wasn’t even Sunday and Rio was dreading that night far more than having to see Agatha. Maybe both were the same amount of nightmare fuel. Fuck. Rio didn’t even want to think about it. 

 

Doomscrolling on her phone, trying to numb the ache in her heart and soothe the upset stomach that hadn’t settled since their fight- A notification from Instagram popped up on the top of her screen, words that made her entire body freeze. 

 

 

Rio stared at the two broken messages. What else was she able to do besides just…stare? 

 

She can’t be talking to me. 

This has to be a mistake.

 

That was it. Just a text to the wrong person. She should lock her phone, drag herself to bed and let Agatha figure out it wasn’t her. 

 

Rio shouldn’t have been surprised how her thumbs tapped the letters off her keyboard, not allowing herself to follow the logical path. Instead, she was going to ask for clarity- See the obvious answer for herself. 

 

 

Holy shit.

She’s drunk. 

Agatha is drunk texting me. 

 

“Oh my god..” Rio mumbled. 

 

And before she could reply, Agatha continued on with a string of messages. 

 

 

We had fun. 

If we matched on Tinder. 

She knows I don’t always hate her-

“Fuck!” Rio harshly whispered. 

 

She quickly sat up in bed, holding her phone tighter as if she could stop Agatha’s messages from coming through. 

 

Rio had to shut this down before she went on any longer. She was drunk, this was all meaningless. Even if the saying was drunken tongue, sober thoughts come out- 

 

Whatever the hell it was, Rio couldn’t figure it out right then and there. Her mind was planning, plotting, flying on a whim to try and put a stop to whatever this conversation was turning into. 

 

 

As much as Rio wanted to shut this down, turn her phone off and disappear into slumber she wished to never wake up from. Not in a suicidal way, but to ignore reality for the rest of her life. 

 

Unfortunately, it was never that easy. Rio’s personality, who she was- It cursed her as it did in the parking lot. Where she felt compelled to help Agatha pick up her belongings, now she felt it was her responsibility to make sure the drunk woman she hated and yet missed was safe. 

 

Rio wasn’t surprised to see the following texts of Agatha admitting to where she was. 

 

 

A bar. 

 

“That’s…not helpful, Agatha” Rio whispered to herself, running a hand through her hair. 

 

She needed more information to work with. There were multiple bars in town, Agatha could possibly not even be in town to find her in one. Rio shook her head, typing as part of her brain begged her to stop. 

 

 

Lou Miller. 

 

The universe had granted her a saving grace for knowing exactly who she was talking about. Lou was an old friend of Rio’s from college. They were still friends, but life had taken them in opposite directions. 

 

At first, relief was the only thing running through her mind. She knew where Agatha was, she would be able to track her down and check on her first hand- Let her eyes lay on her, see the woman was safe. 

 

Drunk, but…safe. 

 

“Fuck, why do I even care?” Rio muttered.

 

She pushed herself out of bed, grabbing a hoodie and a pair of black jeans. Her feet rushed through the house, making sure Nicky was content on the couch while pulling her hair up in a hair clip. If Rio wasn’t so worried, she’d cringe at how much of a mess she looked. Especially seeing Agatha, but..

 

She’s drunk. She won’t even remember any of this.  

 

Rio grabbed her keys, opened her phone back up to shoot Agatha another message. On one side, she wanted to confirm it was Lou she was talking about. On the other, she needed to know Agatha wasn’t so far gone to not reply to her anymore. 

 

 

Why not me? 

She found a way to choke on air, a few coughs as she struggled to shut the front door behind her. Rio held tight onto the doorknob, eyes wide as she stared at the text messages. The previous ones started to sink into her mind as well. 

 

Would you be jealous if I fucked her?

I’d rather fuck you, Rio. 

I shouldn’t say that.

 

“She’s drunk..” Rio told herself, collecting enough strength to make her way to the car while chanting like a mantra, “She’s drunk. She’s drunk. She’s drunk”

 

Shaking her head, feeling her heart racing to the point her pulse thundered up into her throat- Rio managed to tap Lou’s contact while turning the key in the ignition. She put the car in drive, taking off out of her driveway as if she was fleeing a crime scene and needed to escape the police behind her. 

 

The phone rang a few times, on the verge of being met with her voicemail. 

 

“Come on..” Rio muttered, fingers tapping against the steering wheel. 

 

Just as she was about to give up hope, make another plan to drive around incase Agatha managed to leave before she got there-

 

“Rio Vidal, long time since you’ve rang” 

 

The Australian voice rasped with a laugh and Rio let out the longest exhale of relief in her entire life. 

 

“What’s going on?” Lou asked. 

 

“Yeah, hey- Uh, you have a mess of a woman at your bar right now. Wild brown hair, um-” Rio sighed, pinching the bridge of her nose. “I don’t fucking know what she’s wearing…maybe a flannel or-”

 

“Harkness?” 

 

Harkness.  

 

Rio sighed, relieved she located Agatha. “Yeah. Make sure she stays where she is, please?” 

 

Lou didn’t say anything for a moment, worrying Rio she wasn’t currently working or maybe found the request weird. She wouldn’t blame her. Rio was basically asking a friend she hadn't spoken to in ages to keep a random woman hostage. 

 

“How do you know her?” She asked. 

 

Rio shook her head as if Lou was able to see her. 

 

“Long story, not enough time- Just, make sure she doesn’t move and stop serving her” She ordered. 

 

“Sir yes sir..” Lou muttered. 

 

“Thank you, seriously” She sighed. 

 

The phone call ended, leaving Rio to hear the sound of her car and thoughts racing faster than the fifty miles per hour she was flying at. Her grip on the steering wheel tightened, jaw clenched as her fear about Agatha leaving paused for a moment. 

 

The texts started to flicker through her mind, envisioning every single one word for word. There were a few that held their own collection of, holy fuck. But one in particular stood out the most above all. 

 

Rio stopped at the red light, looking around before whispering to herself outloud,

 

“She wants to fuck me?”

 

 

Rio pulled into the tiny parking lot, barely turning the engine off before jumping out of the car. Her body felt on high alert, struck with fear as if she was walking into her death sentence. A firing squad behind the front door, lethal injection that’d be stabbed in her veins the second she stepped through the threshold. Everything felt like a dooming end and yet? 

 

None of it mattered. Rio would walk into fire without a second thought if it meant at the end, Agatha was safe. 

 

This is insane..

 

She ignored her thoughts to push the door open, being welcomed to the grunge atmosphere. Lou wasn’t one for fancy places. She bought the dive bar years ago when her on and off girlfriend had been sentenced to a lengthy prison stay. It was something to distract her, keep her busy and unsurprisingly? She had made a decent name for herself. 

 

Rio scanned each person, looked around the sea of people until her eyes found the crazed brown hair at the bar. The same blue flannel she wore at the rage room, her body slumped with a hand gesturing in the air- probably slurring and rambling on about something. 

 

Too busy threading herself through the crowd of sweaty, drunk, messy people- Rio didn’t register the song that played through the speakers. If she did..well, it’d be another mental curse out for Wanda to shut up about the universe’s signs. Sparks by Coldplay and ironically, Rio didn't even like Coldplay. But if she heard the lyrics, they'd feel way too realistic to what was happening with them both.

 

"Did I drive you away?
I know what you'll say
You say, "Oh, sing one we know"

 

But I promise you this
I'll always look out for you
Yeah, that's what I'll do"

 

Rio reached out, gently placing her hand on Agatha’s shoulder- Thankfully her adrenaline was running its own marathon to ignore how a simple touch felt like a million voltages electrocuting her all at once. 

 

“Aga-”

 

“Well!” Agatha yelled, the words all slurred into one. “Look who it is, everybody!” She waved her arm around, head tilted back as she yelled over the music. “My number one hater!” 

 

Lou walked over, drying the glass in her hand with a small grin. 

 

“Vidal” She greeted. 

 

Rio looked over her shoulder with a nod. 

 

“Thank you” She mouthed. 

 

Lou winked. 

 

“She was about to take off just a few minutes ago, bribed her with a drink” 

 

“Bribe me?!” Agatha laughed. “I can’t be bribed! I’m immortal!”

If she were sober, Rio would totally be making fun of her for how that made zero sense. Instead, she just shook her head while grabbing Agatha’s jacket and purse. 

 

“Come on, I’m taking you home” 

 

Agatha shook her head. 

 

“I’m not done yet and also, no! I’m not spending time with you to go to work tomorrow and you hate me all over again!” 

 

Lou snorted, muttering under her breath. 

 

“Don’t think Sunday means work..”

 

Rio subtly glared back at her, but returned her attention to tug Agatha’s arm towards her. 

 

“Just, please?” Rio asked. “Walk with me at the least” 

 

“Keeping my enemy closeeeee” Agatha giggled. 

 

“Good, that works. Follow the saying” Rio nodded. 

 

Rio managed to help Agatha off the barstool. She pulled her wallet out with one hand, keeping the other holding tight onto the woman’s arm. Lou pushed her wallet back, waving with a low, 

 

“Don’t worry about it. You’ll get me back when we catch up next week?” 

 

She looked up with a thankful smile. 

 

“Get that redheaded witch to join us” She added.

 

Rio snickered. “She’ll be thrilled. Thanks again, Lou”

 

“Good luck” She pointed. “Take care, Harkness!”

 

“Not with her will I!” Agatha’s body slumped against Rio’s with a little giggle. “Hiiii”

 

Rio tried to hold her own grin back, making sure Agatha’s belongings were secure in one hand- Agatha’s physical being locked in the other. 

 

“Come on,” She encouraged. 

 

They stumbled through the bar side by side, but once they got out onto the sidewalk- Agatha almost went face first into the concrete. Rio’s arm lunged out, hooking around her waist and pulling her body right against her own. 

 

Agatha giggled, leaning back into her embrace with a messy, 

 

“My hee- Oh, hero!” 

 

The other woman shook her head, fighting for her life to ignore every warm feeling and swirl of butterflies that started to create a mess of herself. After a few minutes, Rio managed to get Agatha into the passenger seat of her car, thinking about how the roles were exchanged. It wasn’t her in Agatha’s car, but the reverse this time. 

 

And I was sober. She thought to herself.

 

“What’s your address?” Rio asked as she buckled her in. 

 

“What’d you have in mind?” Agatha rasped, wiggling her eyebrows. 

 

Rio sighed, leaning an arm on top of the car with her other hand placed firmly on her hip.

“Get you to bed, that’s-”

 

“Ooo! Scandalous” Agatha giggled. “And then what?” 

 

“Fucks sake..” Rio muttered. 

 

She shut the car door, walking around the front as she tried to figure out what to do about-

 

BEEEEP.

 

“FUCK!” Rio yelled. 

 

Her hand pressed against her chest, eyes wide as her body trembled with the sudden fear. She looked through the windshield to find Agatha leaned over, hands pressing on the horn with a grin so wide- It threatened to stretch her face apart. 

 

The woman rushed to open her car door, pushing the giddy woman away who whined the second Rio sat in the seat beside her. 

 

“You’re no fun!” She pouted.

 

Rio caught her breath, pulling the buckle over her torso with a low scoff, 

 

“My apologies..” She muttered. 

 

Agatha was humming some tune, whispering the words about going down a road. Rio didn’t bother to truly listen. Reality was slowly coming to light, realizing she had no other option without knowing where Agatha lived. 

 

If she called Lilia, Jen, Alice, hell even that William/Billy kid (I really need to figure out his name someday)-  She’d never hear the end of it. And with the fight that had happened between them, would Agatha hate her even more for outting them? 

 

There’s nothing about us to out! Rio yelled in her mind. 

 

She wouldn’t admit to it, but the other half of reality was something far worse than the others tormenting Rio for saving a drunken Agatha-

 

I need to keep her safe. 

What if she hurts herself or gets sick?

 

No- I can’t seriously be debating-

 

“So..where we going, my chauffeur?” Agatha asked.

 

Rio took in a deep breath, turning the key in the ignition as she nodded to herself with the two words that didn’t feel real, 

 

“My place” She answered.

 

Agatha gasped. 

 

“Scanda-”

 

“Lous, yeah. I know” Rio grumbled. 

 

She pulled out of the parking lot, driving down the empty dim lit road with Agatha humming the same tune beside her. Rio hoped it’d stay that way for the rest of the night. By morning, Agatha would most likely take an Uber once she realized where she was. Part of her worried Agatha would kill her for doing this, bringing her to her house intoxicated off her ass. 

 

Rio made a mental note to ask Lou how much she drank once Agatha was settled on the couch.

 

“I’m sorry for fucking it up..y’know?” Agatha muttered. 

 

Rio shook her head. “Agatha, you’re drun-”

 

“Ask me this sober!” She exclaimed. “I never wanted to hate you- hate me- hate us- hate hate HATEEE!” She whined. “Okay?! So..”

 

She stopped at the redlight, taking in a deep breath before looking over to see Agatha’s eyes drooping shut. Her head started to drop, slumber taking over all her words and actions. Part of her was thankful for it, even if getting the woman out of the car may be more difficult. She had silence to collect herself and-

 

Thud. 

 

Rio’s body froze, every muscle tensed while her blood flowing through her came to a stop. The frizzy hair tickled her face, the smell of liquor and that familiar vanilla conditioner hit her like a storm. The weight of Agatha’s head rested on her shoulder, but none of it felt as heavy as Rio’s emotions in that moment. 

 

You hate her. 

 

It felt so right to have Agatha like this.

 

You hate her. 

 

Her giggle was contagious, how she felt warm pressed against her while they stumbled out of the bar together. 

 

You hate her. 

 

And the idea of bringing her home? The feeling of keeping her safe? 

 

You hate her. 

 

“Your shoulder is comfy” Agatha mumbled.

 

Please remember you hate her. Rio begged herself. 

 

Luckily the remainder of the drive home, Agatha didn’t say anything else. She had fallen asleep on Rio’s shoulder, leaving drool on a small part of her hoodie. The woman wouldn’t notice until she took it off to change into a comfy t-shirt later that night. 

 

Every red light felt far too long, when a car pulled out in front of her- They drove too slow. What felt like hours later did her house finally come into vision. Like a beacon of safety shining for them both. 

 

Rio pulled into the driveway, not bothering to back in as she normally would. All she wanted was to get Agatha inside, seclude herself in her bedroom and wait for the most terrifying night of her life to be over. 

 

She gently pushed Agatha’s head up, slipping out of the vehicle. This time Rio walked around the back, not trusting Agatha to stay asleep and not lay into the horn this time. Rio would be giving her hell for that move sober or not. 

 

Rio opened the passenger door, leaning down as she whispered, 

 

“C’mon..”

 

Agatha groaned, mumbling how she was tired and didn't want to move. Rio ignored her, lifting the woman by her hips to stand up. However, the younger woman started to fall side to side, front and back until Rio finally accepted-

 

Agatha walking would be impossible, that was for sure. 

 

Shit. Fine. 

 

Rio mentally counted down from three before hooking one arm under the woman’s legs, the other supporting her back. She couldn’t refrain the little smile on her lips as Agatha’s giggle blew a warm stream of air against her neck, sending chills down her spine. 

 

“My heroooo” She mumbled. 

 

She sighed, mumbling a low. “Yeah, something like that”

 

Rio struggled to unlock the door, but somehow managed to do so and she was thankful for being able to multitask. 

 

Take that, Wanda. Carrying in all the groceries at once pays off. 

 

Nicky greeted them the second she stepped through the threshold. Rio whispered to him to take it easy, not to jump or knock her down while holding Agatha. He was an energetic dog, but luckily listened to Rio well enough to keep his calm. 


She maneuvered through the house, careful to not knock Agatha’s legs or head into anything. Nicky stood to the side, tail wagging, eager to sniff the woman up and down as Rio placed her gently on the couch. 

 

“I know..” Rio smiled softly at him. “New person, that’s rare isn’t it?” She whispered. 

 

Rio never brought anyone home. Only Wanda and Natasha were the two regulars to stop by with the occasional Lilia or Alice. Otherwise, no one ever had access into Rio’s home. She kept the house as her sanctuary safe from the outside world. 

 

Agatha snuggled into the couch more, unfazed by the little sniffles against her arm. Rio moved to take her boots off, gentle to not wake her up. Just as she put them to the side and turned, Nicky was biting onto the fleece blanket and pulling it down from the top of the couch. He draped it over her body, stepping back, giving a proud smile to Rio who’s jaw dropped. 

 

Nicky only ever did that with her. Wanda and Natasha had tried, but he never would budge. The boy had never met Agatha in his entire lifetime and he didn’t hesitate to do something he only ever did for her. 

 

“Suck up” She whispered, ruffling his hair before pressing a kiss on the top of his head. “Come on, I’ll let you outside before bed” 

 

He ran off to the kitchen, leaving Rio alone to make sure Agatha was secured. She told herself to remember water and a bucket in case she woke up sick. But what caught her eye was Agatha’s phone on the table. It lit up with the notification of her battery running low. 

 

Rio hesitated, worried taking it may piss Agatha off more than she possibly would in the morning. But, ultimately Rio took it to plug the device in the kitchen. She had a charger right next to the coffee machine, usually saved for her own. But, Agatha would most likely want to order an Uber before she woke up-n That’d be a good excuse to take it to charge it, no?

 

She opened the door on her way by, letting the boy run free. But as he ran, his leg caught her own and she tripped over with Agatha’s phone flying in the air. Nicky didn’t seem phased, not bothering to turn and make sure Rio hadn’t fallen. Rio usually would joke at him for his selfishness, but she was focused on catching Agatha’s phone in the air and realizing-

 

It was unlocked. 

 

At first, Rio re-locked the phone. She didn't think to snoop or do anything else. There was no point in doing such a thing. But what was something Rio thought to do?

 

Delete those messages. 

 

She had grabbed a bottle of water, searching for a bowl or bucket to place on the floor by Agatha’s head when the thought abruptly entered her mind. Additional thoughts didn’t waste a second to add themselves on like leeches, ready to suck her dry. 

 

She’ll hate you even more seeing those. 

She’ll regret it.

Would she quit? No. I can’t let her do that. 

She can’t leave. 

 

Rio looked over her shoulder at the phone sitting on the counter. The device was charging, minding it’s own business and furthermore-

 

Not my property to do that..

 

She shook her head, continuing to open cabinets and walk around the house, searching for the bucket. However with every second, the thought grew stronger- She felt more scared Agatha would actually quit her job and leave out of embarrassment.

 

I can’t..

 

Rio found the bucket in her bathroom, tucked in the back of her linen closet. She brought both items into the living room, making sure Agatha was still asleep and breathing. Nicky’s paws broke through the silence, tapping against the floor before he jumped up to snuggle himself onto Agatha’s legs. Rio looked over, a tiny grin tugged on her lips as she faked being offended. 

 

“Trader” 

 

She mouthed, leaning down to kiss the top of his head before looking Agatha over one more time. Rio told herself to go to bed, hide in fear for when the woman would sober up and call her a freak, lunatic, every word in the book for bringing her home. Her bedroom would be safe..well, she hoped anyway. 


Rio walked through the kitchen, making sure the backyard door was shut and locked. Just as she turned the kitchen light off, Agatha’s phone screen lit up in the darkness with a notification. 

 

Walk away. Don’t do it. 

 

She bit the inside of her cheeks, nodding to herself as she stormed off to her bedroom. However, Rio only got to the door when her anxiety pushed her back like a gust of wind stronger than nature itself could ever create. The woman almost tripped over her feet to get back to the phone, looking over her shoulder to make sure Agatha wasn’t behind her. 

 

Opening the Instagram app, Rio told herself she wouldn’t delete them all. Just the ones that Agatha may regret, make sure to tell Rio how disgusting those ideas sounded. 

 

“I think if we matched on Tinder” - Deleted.

 

“Wasting time on you” - Deleted.

 

“Would you be jealous if I fucked her?” - Deleted.

 

“I’d rather fuck you” - Deleted. 

 

“Did you fuck her?” - Deleted.

 

“Why not me?” - Deleted. 

 

Rio exited the app, locking the screen and placed the phone back down. She stepped away, hand over her mouth while the other gripped the end of her sleeve so hard she threatened to tear through the fabric. 

 

Agatha Harkness, her worst enemy and slowly becoming her worst crush of a lifetime, passed out drunk on her couch. Rio had just violated her phone, deleted messages that now would live in Rio’s mind alone. She’d have to think about them twenty four seven, being the only one between the two to ever know they existed. 

 

Her lips parted, jaw slacked as she felt her eyes stinging with tears filled with fear,

 

What the fuck did you just do?
